                            <div class="player-info-box-header team-cardinals"><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Yadier Molina</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team"><a href="/teams/cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a></div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 35</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: R/R</div>

        <div class="player-info-box-pos">C</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>7/13/1982 (35 y, 7 m, 25 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=7007&position=C#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2000 June Amateur Draft - Round: 4, Pick: 13, Overall: 113, Team: St. Louis Cardinals</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=7007&position=C#contract" >$60M / 3 Years (2018 - 2020)</a>

                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=7501">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Molina is slashing .167/.231/.417 with a solo home run, a walk and two runs over 13 plate appearances in five spring training games. (3/5/2018)</div></td></tr>

        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>Known more for his ability to gun down runners and call a game from behind the plate, Molina turned in a solid fantasy season in 2009. Hitting .293/.366/.383 with a wOBA of .337, he added six homers while driving in 54 runs for the Cardinals. He also scored 45 runs and stole nine bases in 544 plate appearances. Molina is one of the rare hitters who walks more than he strikes out, taking first base 50 times in 2009 while only striking out on 39 occasions. From behind the plate, Molina threw out 22 runners while allowing 32 steals on the year, the fewest number in the entire Major Leagues. <br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Molina’s new-found speed was a special treat for his owners, as he had never stolen more than two bags in any previous season. Unfortunately, it may be a fluke, so don’t expect him to continue to increase those results in 2010. In essence, Molina is a catcher who you would draft if you aren’t worried about getting much production from his position, and just want a player who won’t kill your batting average. He isn’t a run scorer or producer and doesn’t have much power to speak of, but he won’t hurt your team like other catchers tend to do. If you want to focus on other positions in your draft, Molina is a nice late option to fill out your roster. (Zach Sanders)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Yadier Molina is a very good baseball player.  He would be an important piece for any franchise, thanks to his remarkable defense at the catcher position.  However, thanks to his deficiencies at the plate, his fantasy value is limited to the position that he plays.  What we saw from Molina in 2010 is essentially what we've gotten his whole career: a middling batting average, 35-45 runs, 50-65 RBIs, six or seven homers, and, somehow, almost 10 SBs the last two seasons.  There's no reason to expect much to change next season.  Molina will continue to draw a moderate amount of walks and make contact at a high rate.  Power will continue to elude Molina as well.  However, thanks to the dearth of productive catchers around the league, Molina has some value.  He will pick up a lot of plate appearances, which makes playing time less of a concern than with many other catchers.  That combination of production and playing time makes him a good player in deeper leagues and particularly NL-only leagues, and perhaps serves to illustrate just why if you don't get an elite catcher early, you can wait until very late in the draft to fill the position. (Jack Moore)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>For as good of a catcher as Yadier Molina is, he has some struggles at the plate.  He's pretty mediocre everywhere, and although that can play at catcher, his fantasy value is small.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>For the first time in his Major League career, Molina smacked double digits in homers, and he set several other bests in both conventional and advanced stat categories. While he probably hit a little bit over his head last season, he is above-average offensively for a catcher. And just as importantly, because he is above-average defensively (above average may be an understatement, actually) he starts the lion’s share of games -- last season, he led catchers with 132 games started, and was one of just six to start more than 125 -- and thus drafting Molina means you don’t need to waste a roster spot on a backup catcher. If the power spike is real -- his .160 isolated slugging was double his 2010 mark and was easily a career high -- Molina will once again be a top-10 catcher. (Paul Swydan)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Molina doesn’t have a reputation as a good hitter, but that’s what he was last season, and if you miss out on the top catchers, he should be a good fallback option.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Like a fine wine, Molina continues to get better and better with age. Most expected the Cardinals backstop, who turned 30 during the middle of the 2012 season, to have reached his peak during his breakout 2011 campaign, but he turned right around and set new career highs in every one of the five basic roto categories, as well as on-base percentage, slugging and wOBA. He easily produced a season worthy of consideration amongst the top five catchers in the game. Given the fact that his .189 isolated slugging percentage last year was considerably higher than his career average, it's difficult to expect a return to the 20-home run plateau, however, with such outstanding plate discipline and such a strong read on opposing pitchers, you can probably expect his remaining totals to be comparable to what we've seen over the past two seasons. His price tag continues to rise, but with the way he has produced lately, it's hard to say he isn't worth it. (Howard Bender)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Just when you thought you couldn't squeeze any more out of Molina, he turns around and improves even more on his 2011 breakout campaign. His 2012 totals moved him into the top tier of backstops, with his .315 average, 22 home runs and 12 stolen bases. He might not reach the 20-home run mark again this year, but the rest of his numbers should make him worthy of his higher draft position.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Despite some slight regression off his career offensive season in 2012, Molina was once again a top fantasy catcher. His power fell off as expected, but excellent contact combined with tons of line drives that boosted his batting average on balls in play ensured he hit above .300 for the third straight year. At age 31 and with knee issues cropping up, it appears rather safe to figure that his days of high single-digit to double-digit steals are over. Though he has remained rather consistent these past three years, some warning signs are creeping up. He has been swinging and missing a little more often than usual since 2012, and his strikeout rate reached its highest mark since 2007. I would be hesitant to pay full value given the risk of BABIP decline and aging effects taking their toll. (<a href="https://twitter.com/MikePodhorzer" target="_blank">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Molina remained a strong fantasy catcher for a third straight season, but there are several warning signs worth heeding. Since catchers are always risky to begin with, paying top dollar for a 31 year old with sudden knee issues is probably unwise.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Yadier Molina had a career year with 22 home runs in 2012, but he has declined to 12 home runs in 2013 and just seven in 2014. It’s easy to view those 22 home runs the way we do Joe Mauer’s 28 home run season, especially now that Molina is 32 years old. However, it’s important to consider that Molina’s 2014 season was derailed by a thumb injury that required surgery and cost him more than a month on the disabled list. Meanwhile, Molina hit all seven of his home runs in the first half, before the thumb injury. It’s not a stretch to think that Molina could hit close to 20 home runs, again, and with his consistency in terms of batting average and his high games played — thumb injury aside — compared to most catchers, he is a clear top five player at the position. (Scott Spratt)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Molina missed time with a thumb injury in 2014 that also cost him his power. Expect a bounce back in 2015, which makes him a clear top five catcher.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>For much of his career, Molina has been a catching iron man. The best of the Molina brothers, Yadier had an excellent three-year peak from 2011 through 2013. Injuries have slowed him in recent seasons, and it's fair to expect that trend to continue. Now 33, Molina has a lot of mileage on his body. Last year, he played through a thumb injury. He's expected to miss most of spring training recovering from surgery. Even with a hurt hand, Molina still posted above average contact numbers. The issue was his utter lack of power. As a result, he had his worst season since 2006. There's a chance Molina has one or two more renaissance campaigns left in the tank. I wouldn't expect 2016 to be one of them. (Brad Johnson)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>After two seasons affected by thumb injuries, Molina is expected to get a late start in Spring Training. The chance for a rebound campaign exists, but it's safer to expect contact skills, strong defense, and little else.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After a down year, Yadier Molina bounced back in 2016 to put up above average offensive numbers. Many of his peripheral stats, SwStrk%, K%, BB%, GB%, and FB% have remained pretty consistent in recent years. It appears his 2015 dip had more to do with a sudden drop in Exit Velocity, which dropped to 86 mph, 2 mph below average. In 2016, this exit velocity bounced back to 88 mph and with it came Yadi’s power. Starting with the bad, Molina suffered a 51 day, 47 game slump from May 17 through July 7th in which he bat .190/.238/.229 with a wRC+ of 24. It appears this slump may have been more due to a little bad luck as opposed to any sort of major red flag. For much of the season, if you exclude that slump, Yadi posted a slugging hovering around the .500 mark. Above .500, in fact, from July through October. This in addition to a .392 OBP cemented Yadier Molina as one of the most valuable players in the second half of 2016 where he ranked 10th in wOBA (.392) and 7th in wRC+ (150). For the season, he registered the lowest K% of all catchers with at least 250 PA, and the fourth lowest SwStrk%. Yadier Molina proved he is still one of the most valuable catchers in MLB and a valuable asset for any fantasy team. (Andrew Perpetua)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Yadier Molina was held back by injuries to his legs and hands in 2015, but those injuries have healed. Age is catching up to him and his skills are diminishing, but he remains a top 15 catcher, perhaps even top 10.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
